Causality and Created Things
intermediate
4 min
The Second Proof and Its Refutation
Ghazali presents and refutes the philosophers' second proof for the impossibility of non-existence of substances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' second proof for the impossibility of non-existence of substances and Ghazali's refutation based on the concept of possibility.

Core Idea
The philosophers' second proof confuses possibility with a physical substrate.

In this passage, Ghazali presents the second proof offered by the philosophers for the impossibility of non-existence of substances. He then refutes it concisely by referring back to his earlier arguments. The key point is that the philosophers treat possibility as requiring a substrate, which has already been dismantled in the discussion on the eternity of the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the philosopher's claim and Ghazali's response sink in.
Pay attention to the phrase 'فيستحيل عليه العدم'.
2
Identify the proof
Find the statement that constitutes the philosophers' second proof. It is a conditional statement about substances not in a subject.
The proof claims impossibility of non-existence.
3
Understand Ghazali's refutation
Notice that Ghazali does not give a new argument but refers to earlier discussions. The core issue is their treatment of possibility.
He says the source of obfuscation is their positing possibility as requiring a substrate.
4
Reflect on the concept of possibility
Consider why possibility does not need a substrate. This is a key distinction between kalam and philosophy.
Ghazali's earlier refutation is considered sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدليل الثاني : قولهم : كل جوهر ليس في محل فيستحيل عليه العدم . قال الغزالي في رد هذا الدليل : ويدفع هذا بما قررناه في ذهابهم إلى استحالة حدوث المادة والعناصر ، واستحالة عدمها، في مسألتي أزلية العالم وأبديته المسألة ، ومنشأ التلبيس وضعهم الإمكان وضعاً مستدعياً محلا يقوم به ، وقد تكلمنا عليه بما فيه مقنع ، فلا نعيده ؛ فإن المسألة هی ولا فرق بين أن يكون المتكلم فيه ، جوهر مادة ، أو جوهر نفس
The second proof: Their statement: Every substance that is not in a subject is impossible to undergo non-existence. Al-Ghazali said in refuting this proof: This is repelled by what we established in [the discussion of] their view of the impossibility of the occurrence of matter and elements, and the impossibility of their non-existence, in the two issues of the eternity of the world and its perpetuity. The source of obfuscation is their positing possibility as requiring a substrate to subsist in, and we have discussed it sufficiently, so we will not repeat it; for the issue is the same, and there is no difference whether what is spoken of is the substance of matter or the substance of the soul.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage contains a brief proof offered by the philosophers and Ghazali's response. The proof states: every substance not existing in a subject (i.e., a simple substance like the soul) cannot cease to exist; it is necessary. Ghazali refutes this by saying that this has already been answered in his earlier discussion of the philosophers' views on the eternity of the world. The mistake, he says, is that they treat 'possibility' as if it requires a physical substrate to inhere in, but that has been sufficiently refuted. He adds that there is no difference between the substance of matter and the substance of the soul in this regard. Thus, he does not need to repeat the argument here.

Key Terms
جوهر
محل
إمكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility (imkan) requires a physical substrate to inhere in for a thing to be considered possible.
Correction: Ghazali argues that possibility does not need a substrate; it is a rational judgment about the thing itself.

Checkpoint
What is the second proof of the philosophers according to Ghazali in this passage?
A) Every body is composed of atoms.
B) Every substance not in a subject is impossible to non-exist.
C) The soul is eternal.
D) Matter is uncreated.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' second proof fails because possibility does not require a substrate, a point Ghazali had already established.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever trusted a rational argument about your soul's immortality without examining its hidden assumptions? What might you be assuming about 'proof' that this lesson challenges you to question?
?
The philosophers' error was treating an intellectual concept (possibility) as if it needed a physical location. In what areas of your faith do you similarly demand physical evidence for spiritual truths? Will you repent of that demand and submit to the Quran's teachings instead?
?
Ghazali says the issue is the same for matter and the soul. If you truly believed your soul is as contingent as a speck of dust, would your priorities change? How does this lesson move you to rely solely on Allah's will for your existence, not on rational necessity?
